  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5eb5a420-c200-4841-9f17-ae72a34f4c88'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer2759371320216213343">I started reading the first line and I knew immediately that I would be unable to put the book down long after the last words. This is Marc Levy at his finest.<br/> <br/>Love is there everywhere, not the kind of sweet, dramatic love in his other works but the most simple, natural, essential kinds of love. Throughout the war, through joy and pain, through tears and blood, though life and death, there is still love.<br/><br/>The name and cover are really great. They suit the book perfectly.</span>

<div id="review_143993940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143993940" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Carmo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Carmo" href="/user/show/3054983-maria-carmo">Maria Carmo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3054983-maria-carmo?shelf=novel-romance-revealing-historica">novel-romance-revealing-historica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3054983-maria-carmo?shelf=living-theend-times">living-theend-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3054983-maria-carmo?shelf=life-changing-self-discovery-self">life-changing-self-discovery-self</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143993940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3837292099019690177">This is an OUTSTANDING book, so true and inspiring for the great examples of life and generosity of these youth who were part of the French Resistance! It is incredible to think that they were young boys and girls of 17 to 20 years old, and what sacrifices they made for a country that, in many cases, wasn't their country of origin. Through the book, there is one moment when they are going to be arrested by the collaborationist government (who is collaborating with Nazi Germany) and they could ha</span>
  <span id="freeText3837292099019690177" style="display:none">This is an OUTSTANDING book, so true and inspiring for the great examples of life and generosity of these youth who were part of the French Resistance! It is incredible to think that they were young boys and girls of 17 to 20 years old, and what sacrifices they made for a country that, in many cases, wasn't their country of origin. Through the book, there is one moment when they are going to be arrested by the collaborationist government (who is collaborating with Nazi Germany) and they could have been saved, if not for someone who said: "they are not even French, the Liberation is coming and then France needs French heroes" - No comments!!!!!!!!!! How can anyone be so insensitive and selfish?! Did they deserve the sacrifice of these young men and girls? Some hours later, all of the 35th Brigade fell, even the girls were tortured... Shame on people who do not honour those who are generous to the point of giving their life! Also, in French prisons, these young resistant were shot or even guillotined! And the hatred of both Nazis and Collaborationists was so great, that they tried to deport them to concentrations camps until the very end of the Liberation in France.<br />Thank God there were those who managed to escape the phantom train to stay alive and tell the story! And later, much later, FRANCE decorated the surviving members of the 35th Brigade.<br /><br />Maria Carmo,<br /><br />Lisbon 10 August 2014. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3837292099019690177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170922524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3252472459645283385">A novel that is totally different from all other Marc Levy's novels. This novel doesn't talk about the kind of love that Marc Levy always so passionate tells in his story. This story also tells story about love but a completely distinguish kind of love - the love for their country - the patriotism. I dont think this is a good book at first, but then it was so good that I even cry in the end. This book is just simply good and amazing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16447030694777236642">When I was 17, I wasn't fighting with an underground resistance group in France. But, in WWII, hundreds of teenagers were part of a secretive, starving group of kids who blew up all kinds of German war-related necessities like locomotives and factories making ammunition.   <span id="freeText16447030694777236642" style="display:none">When I was 17, I wasn't fighting with an underground resistance group in France. But, in WWII, hundreds of teenagers were part of a secretive, starving group of kids who blew up all kinds of German war-related necessities like locomotives and factories making ammunition. Yes, they also killed, while carefully avoiding injuring innocents. <br /><br />Eventually, most were caught, beaten, starved and eventually killed. The whole time, they kept the secrets needed for their mission to continue. Along the way, they were helped by brave passers-by and faced up to a heartless enemy - except for the occasional furtive act of kindness from someone from the enemy side. This is a novel that reads like a diary of two brothers. It is based on true stories from those who lived it. <br /><br />As much as it is a chronicle of events, it also shows the love, friendship, and incredible bravery of these young boys and girls on a mission to stop injustice to the best of their ability. I kept thinking that the least we can do as adults is to speak up when we see injustice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16447030694777236642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

This is the story of the 35th regiment of the French resistance, a group made up of communist, spaniards, mixed europeans and Jews.   <span id="freeText8191309702942660359" style="display:none">How can I say this... this is a truly magnificent book. Well written, passionate and heartbreaking. This is the story of the 35th regiment of the French resistance, a group made up of communist, spaniards, mixed europeans and Jews. Marc Levy, in writing this book, accomplished the wishes of the Resistant fighters. He immortalized their struggle and their sacrifice. The main character Jeannot, is actually his father. These are the unsung heroes of the II world war. They were children, they were the target of the Gestapo, the weak races, and yet they fought with what little they had. If nothing else, they accomplished to remain human, in an ugly world. But this book also shows all the other people who continued living their lives... and yet did their part in helping bring down the Third...Reight... the struggle to remain human amidst the horror of wars is what continues to give me hope.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51505705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4902769676867903778">It was a good book overall. The feeling it perpetuates is fairly straighforward and not very nuanced. I wish there was a little more character development, especially toward the end, it reads more like a teletype than a fiction piece. Definitely a decent read those, I will be reading more by this author in the future.<br/> </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Christie Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7901004-christie-adams"><img alt="Christie Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605124176p2/7901004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2195482726?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christie Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christie Adams" href="/user/show/7901004-christie-adams">Christie Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780007274956" href="/book/show/3407728-the-children-of-freedom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2195482726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15545545869259547637">Wow, that took a while! Sadly I couldn’t get along with this book. The subject, smashing, the story good too but the first quarter and beyond were hard to read. I’m not sure if it’s the voice, the translation or narrative but I admit I struggled. Great character though, I did need to know what happened. This era must continue to be in our literature. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286119643?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha Ghawi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha Ghawi" href="/user/show/5091360-natasha-ghawi">Natasha Ghawi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286119643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1186823867180800331">I found it hard to put this book down. It captures you from the first page and keeps you wanting to know more until the last page. Marc Levy is a very talented writer. The book is written during the second world war. It is placed in France when Germany was taking over France. Foreigners were robbed from their right to freedom. The book is mainly about a group of people who are protesting, they are trying to fight for their freedom. Most of them get caught and even when they get caught they still</span>
  <span id="freeText1186823867180800331" style="display:none">I found it hard to put this book down. It captures you from the first page and keeps you wanting to know more until the last page. Marc Levy is a very talented writer. The book is written during the second world war. It is placed in France when Germany was taking over France. Foreigners were robbed from their right to freedom. The book is mainly about a group of people who are protesting, they are trying to fight for their freedom. Most of them get caught and even when they get caught they still fight, the book shows you that no matter what fight for what you believe in. The main character Jeannot and his little brother Claude are both protesting and they both get caught. When they are sent to jail and are beaten up the reader feels as if they are in the cell with them watching them get beaten. Towards the end of the book all political prisoners and handed over to the Nazi officers who will take them to Germany and they will be placed in Death camps. However the Nazi officers move very slowly because they are afraid of the resistance groups to come and bomb them. When they were transporting the political prisoners such as Jeannot and Claude the Nazi officers treated them like animals. They were given food and water every few days and many prisoners died of starvation. After two months of living on this train Jeannot, Claude and a few other people planned an escape. It was successful and they had gotten away. A few day later France was free and the war was over. The foreigners in death camps were let out and given their freedom back. I recommend anyone who likes books on historic fiction to read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1186823867180800331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_607129019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sunnydreamer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4208975-sunnydreamer"><img alt="Sunnydreamer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538905385p2/4208975.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sunnydreamer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sunnydreamer" href="/user/show/4208975-sunnydreamer">Sunnydreamer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer607129019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15102952867860985265">What does <i>resistance</i> mean in the context of war, invasion & occupation?<br/><br/>This is a question answered so powerfully and poignantly in Marc Levy's Les enfants de la liberté ('The Children of Freedom').<br/><br/>I have long been fascinated by the history of the French Resistance, and have read many a compelling book featuring the heroic, humbling actions of that movement. Levy's Les enfants de la liberté must surely now top that list!<br/><br/>I have, over the years, so often pondered my own potential bravery in a simil</span>
  <span id="freeText15102952867860985265" style="display:none">What does <i>resistance</i> mean in the context of war, invasion &amp; occupation?<br /><br />This is a question answered so powerfully and poignantly in Marc Levy's Les enfants de la liberté ('The Children of Freedom').<br /><br />I have long been fascinated by the history of the French Resistance, and have read many a compelling book featuring the heroic, humbling actions of that movement. Levy's Les enfants de la liberté must surely now top that list!<br /><br />I have, over the years, so often pondered my own potential bravery in a similar context of war, occupation and persecution. Would I remain a mere bystander to such atrocious acts of evil - fearing for my own safety first and foremost - or would I count myself among the brave souls who resisted, for freedom's sake? Would I find the courage to shelter, aid, and abet?<br /><br />It is, after all, the courage and determination of mere civilians-turned-freedom fighters which makes this book so enthralling, heart-stopping and memorable. The achievements of the French Resistance were many and important in the turning of the Second World War, but that success began first in the hearts of individuals like you and I; their willingness to <i>resist.</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15102952867860985265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer487386699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7429648477340985066">This book, which is a translation, and is based on true stories of the period from the father and uncle of the author, reminds us how lucky we are if we are living in a free and democratic society. It outlines conditions in occupied France and the brave actions of the young people of 35th FTP-MOI Brigade of the Resistance, many of them refugees, to frustrate German initiatives and enhance the possibilities for an allied invasion and ultimate defeat of Nazi Germany. One is moved to read about the</span>
  <span id="freeText7429648477340985066" style="display:none">This book, which is a translation, and is based on true stories of the period from the father and uncle of the author, reminds us how lucky we are if we are living in a free and democratic society. It outlines conditions in occupied France and the brave actions of the young people of 35th FTP-MOI Brigade of the Resistance, many of them refugees, to frustrate German initiatives and enhance the possibilities for an allied invasion and ultimate defeat of Nazi Germany. One is moved to read about the risks taken and sacrifices made valiantly by so many as members of the French Resistance. It also brings home the horrors of the period for political prisoners and Jews and the senseless fear, violence and murder which marked this period in history for everyone. This book is definitely worth the read. I feel that the author has fulfilled the promise made by Jeannot to Samuel to ensure that future generations know about and understand the sacrifices made by so many in the fight for freedom during this dark time in history. </span>

    <a title="Joanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3036093-joanna"><img alt="Joanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465290301p2/3036093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684524171?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna" href="/user/show/3036093-joanna">Joanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684524171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1453072030673669819"><i>"If we join the Resistance, it's to live, not to die."</i> This book gives homage to the young men and women who were ready to die for freedom during WWII; those young men and women who bravely fought with the goal of restoring <i>humanity</i> in a world defined by hate and cruelty. Two young Jewish brothers join the 35th Brigade of the French Resistance and this is their story. It is a moving story of resistance, courage, struggle and the "overwhelmingly instinct for survival" (Le Monde). I really enjoyed</span>
  <span id="freeText1453072030673669819" style="display:none"><i>"If we join the Resistance, it's to live, not to die."</i> This book gives homage to the young men and women who were ready to die for freedom during WWII; those young men and women who bravely fought with the goal of restoring <i>humanity</i> in a world defined by hate and cruelty. Two young Jewish brothers join the 35th Brigade of the French Resistance and this is their story. It is a moving story of resistance, courage, struggle and the "overwhelmingly instinct for survival" (Le Monde). I really enjoyed the book and finished it in a week end. The beginning, however, went a little fast for me. I felt that a lot of facts and events were being cited but the development of characters was lacking. As the book goes on, the author makes up for that by delving deeper into the characters and their dynamics with one another. It is a sad but inspiring story that speaks to our power as humans to fight for humanity rather than accept inhumanity. A relevant story in our time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1453072030673669819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1928173142025067772" style="display:none">Just read this on holiday. Found it interesting and it left me with a mixture of emotions. Its one of those historical periods that you struggle to believe actually happened. The war and how it affected so many peoples lives is brought back in vivid detail as we follow a group of resistance fighters. It was heroic, sad, uplifting , funny in parts but above all the bravery of the characters stood out amidst the terror and mayhem of the period. The actions of these people went along way to shortening the war and preventing the deaths of many more. For our freedom today I am eternally grateful - these were people who will always be remembered. Easy to read and one that will linger in the memory for a long time.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ym5QpNleq+wFxkuYErhfnJlllTe4zntNxUetololzbMvSnuaV0Z8AOhQikVrKoqCH3BmsqXLlV4AhuLpTdO1ig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qd27LlwjaaKxK6/uOGD5a5pdLpCDFeaJwQ2dUQ/cDEqk+ZAQ0ju+Tly9bjNB8ix1HEjdFZ4QCJoEzNIaGCp0cw==')})
  }

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_44131365').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61788.Marc_Levy">About Marc Levy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/61788.Marc_Levy"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1359481082p3/61788.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13465602915808332114">Marc Levy was born in France. When he turned eighteen, he joined the Red Cross, where he spent the next six years. In 1983, he created a computer graphics company based in France and the United States. Six years later, he co-founded an interior design and planning company with two friends; the company soon became one of the leading architecture firms in France.<br/><br/>At thirty-seven, Marc Levy wrote a st</span>
  <span id="freeText13465602915808332114" style="display:none">Marc Levy was born in France. When he turned eighteen, he joined the Red Cross, where he spent the next six years. In 1983, he created a computer graphics company based in France and the United States. Six years later, he co-founded an interior design and planning company with two friends; the company soon became one of the leading architecture firms in France.<br /><br />At thirty-seven, Marc Levy wrote a story for the man that his son would grow up to be. In early 1999, his sister, a screenwriter (now a film director), encouraged him to send the manuscript to a French publisher, who immediately decided to publish If Only It Were True. Before it was published, Steven Spielberg (Dreamworks) acquired film rights to the novel. The movie, Just like Heaven, starring Reese Witherspoon and Mark Ruffalo, was a #1 box office hit in America in 2005.<br /><br />After If Only It Were True, Marc Levy began writing full-time. Since then, he has written 18 novels. His work has been translated into 49 languages and has sold over 40 million copies worldwide. <br /><br />In addition, Marc Levy has directed a short movie, written short stories and song lyrics for various artists, including Johnny Hallyday.<br /><br />Le Figaro newspaper recently commissioned a nationwide poll asking the French to rank their favorite author: Marc Levy and Victor Hugo were #1.<br /><br />Marc Levy currently lives in New York City. Readers can learn more about him and follow his work on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marclevy.info">www.marclevy.info</a> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13465602915808332114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1461231-les-enfants-de-la-libert">Quotes from Les Enfants de la...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Ecco, amore mio. Quell’uomo elegante con i gomiti appoggiati al bancone del caff des Tourneurs, che ti sorride, è mio padre. Sotto la terra di Francia riposano i tuoi compagni. Ogni volta che sento qualcuno esprimere le proprie idee in un mondo libero, penso a loro. Allora mi ricordo che la parola «straniero» è una delle più belle promesse del mondo, una promessa a colori, bella come la Libertà&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/440799-ecco-amore-mio-quell-uomo-elegante-con-i-gomiti-appoggiati-al">4 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Cela pose un problème que...?"<br />"Que tu ne sois pas juif? Pas le moins du tout, dit maman en riant. Ni mon mari ni moi n'accordons d'importance à la différence de l'autre. Bien au contraire, nous avons toujours pensé que'elle était passionnante et source de multiples bonheurs. Le plus important, quand on veut vivre à deux toute une vie, est d'etre sur que l'on ne s'ennuiera pas ensemble. L'ennui dans un couple, c'est lui qui tue l'amour. Tant que tu feras rire Alice, tant que tu lui donneras l'envie de te retrouver, alors que tu viens à peine de la quitter pour aller travailler, tant que tu seras celui dont elle partage les confidences et à qui elle aime aussi se confier, tant que tu vivras tes reves avec elle, meme ceux que tu ne pourras pas réaliser, alors je suis certaine que quelles que soient tes origines, la seule chose qui sera étrangère à votre couple sera le monde et ses jaloux.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/545977-cela-pose-un-probl-me-que-que-tu-ne-sois-pas">3 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
